L. K. Comstock & Co. v. New York Convention Center Dev. Corp.


44951


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


179 A.D.2d 322; 584 N.Y.S.2d 472; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6651



May 7, 1992, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which denied its motion to strike the fourth counterclaim asserted in defendant city development corporation's answer in plaintiff's breach of contract action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contractors filed a breach of contract action against defendant city development corporation for contracting work. Plaintiff sought damages on the contract, delay, and inefficiency damages. Defendant asserted affirmative defenses and filed counterclaims. Plaintiff sought partial summary judgment dismissing defendant's fourth counterclaim, alleging that plaintiff failed to provide for participation by minority business enterprises (MBE) as promised, and was not entitled to the monies. The motion court denied summary judgment because there were issues of fact about the liquidated damages clause and allegations concerning the principals' minority status. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that plaintiff's challenge to the MBE program arose solely in response to allegations that the contracts plaintiff sought to enforce were awarded based upon plaintiff's misrepresentation of MBE compliance. The court held that plaintiff's challenge to the program after 10 years of participation and $ 46 million in payments to plaintiff was untenable, because the court found a voluntary, knowing and intelligent waiver of constitutional rights based upon plaintiff's participation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of summary judgment by the motion court, holding that plaintiff contractor's challenge to the minority business enterprise program arose solely in response to allegations that the contracts plaintiff sought to enforce were awarded based upon plaintiff's misrepresentation of MBE compliance. Plaintiff's challenge to the program after 10 years of participation and $ 46 million in payments to plaintiff was waived.

 

453 of 992 DOCUMENTS


East Hampton v. Cuomo


92-01834, 92-02018


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


179 A.D.2d 337; 583 N.Y.S.2d 968; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6739


April 8, 1992, Argued  
May 4, 1992, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff towns and defendants, a Governor and a Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Conservation (State), cross-appealed a judgment from the Suffolk County Supreme Court (New York) entered in litigation under the Long Island Landfill Law, N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law § 27-0704.


OVERVIEW: To preserve Long Island's sole source aquifer, § 27-0704 mandated the closure of the landfill on which the towns relied. The towns filed suit, alleging the unconstitutionality of the statute as applied to them, to which the State responded with a motion for summary judgment that was later denied. Although the parties cross-appealed concerning a subpoena served upon the Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Conservation (DEC), the court mooted that issue by granting the State's motion for summary judgment. The court held that: (1) the towns' summary judgment proof failed to rebut the strong presumption of constitutionality that attended § 27-0704; (2) the towns' statutory duty to close their landfills was independent of the DEC's charge to issue a solid waste management policy for Long Island; (3) the towns' summary judgment evidence raised no issues of fact as to whether the Commissioner changed one town's hydrologic zone boundaries; and (4) even if the towns' summary judgment proof did raise a fact issue on that question, the State was still entitled to summary judgment because, under the statute, the Commissioner had authority to change hydrologic zone boundaries.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court order that denied the State's motion for summary judgment, entered a summary judgment for the State, and dismissed the parties' cross-appeal of the trial court's order regarding the subpoena issued to the Commissioner.

 

454 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Regan v. Cuomo


64797


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


182 A.D.2d 1060; 583 N.Y.S.2d 41; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6437



April 30, 1992, Decided  
April 30, 1992, Entered



DISPOSITION: ORDERED that the order is affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Governor of the State of New York, Budget Director of the State of New York (director), and other state officials, appealed an order of the Supreme Court for Albany County (New York), which denied defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint for lack of standing in a declaratory judgment action by plaintiff Comptroller of the State of New York (comptroller) challenging the constitutionality of N.Y. Pub. Auth. Law § 381.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature enacted § 381, which authorized the New York State Thruway Authority (authority) to issue bonds, entitled the authority to pledge contracts as security for its bonds, and granted the director power to obligate the state to provide payments to fund the debt on the bonds. The comptroller brought an action against defendants, seeking a declaration that § 381 was unconstitutional. Defendants brought a motion to dismiss on the ground that the comptroller lacked standing, that the controversy was not justiciable, and that the comptroller failed to obtain approval of the action from the state attorney general as required under N.Y. Exec. Law § 63. The trial court denied the motion, and defendants appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the comptroller, who had the duty to oversee the state's fiscal concerns, had an actual legal stake in the matter. The action was justiciable because declaratory judgment actions were commonly used to determine the rights of parties upon the happening of a future event. The comptroller did not need approval to bring the action because his capacity to do so was implied from the powers granted him by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint for lack of standing, in the comptroller's declaratory judgment action against defendants challenging the constitutionality of a state law.

 

455 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Prop. Clerk v. Molomo


44488


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


179 A.D.2d 210; 583 N.Y.S.2d 251; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6280



April 23, 1992, Decided  
April 23, 1992, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant police department property clerk challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which awarded possession of defendant car owner's forfeited vehicle to plaintiff lienholder and enjoined the lienholder from allowing the car owner to redeem the vehicle.


OVERVIEW: After the owner of a car was charged with criminal possession of narcotics, his vehicle was seized as an instrumentality of crime. The police department property clerk appealed the award of possession of the vehicle to the lienholder of the vehicle. On appeal, the court modified the lower court's judgment. The court held that the lienholder was not entitled to the right to replevin of the vehicle to satisfy its perfected security interest. The property clerk was permitted to sell the vehicle at auction and retain a portion of the proceeds for administrative expenses. The remainder would be remitted to the lienholder. The court found that the lienholder was not entitled to possession of the vehicle even though the proceeds from the sale would not satisfy the lien, and the lienholder had done all that it reasonably could to prevent the illegal use of the vehicle. As a lienholder, it had no greater right to possession of the vehicle than the owner who had forfeited such right. In addition, the court determined that the lienholder could have insured itself for any loss that it would sustain in the event that a buyer violated a law thus triggering the forfeiture provisions.


OUTCOME: The court modified the lower court's judgment. The lienholder was not entitled to possession of the car, but was entitled to the proceeds from the sale of the car after the property clerk retained a portion for administrative expenses.

 

456 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Banfi Prods. Corp. v. O'Cleireacain


45303


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


182 A.D.2d 465; 582 N.Y.S.2d 695; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6017



April 14, 1992, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of an order of the Supreme Court of New York County (New York), that dismissed its declaratory judgment action and denied a motion for a preliminary injunction in its action against defendants, a city agency and its tax commissioner, in which plaintiff contended that defendants' enforcement of the general corporation tax was unconstitutional and in excess of the authority granted by the legislature.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the city's argument that by proceeding before the finance department, the taxpayer elected its remedy was simply erroneous. The court noted that the taxpayer's complaint challenged the constitutionality of the application of the taxation statute by the finance department on equal protection and due process grounds, as well as alleged that the city agency exceeded its statutory authority. The court indicated that even when a taxpayer has received an administrative determination, it may nevertheless attack the constitutionality of a statute in a plenary action. However, the court found that the taxpayer's motion for preliminary injunctive relief presented insufficient evidence to demonstrate a likelihood of success on the merits and made only a conclusory allegation that it would be irreparably injured if injunctive relief was not provided.


OUTCOME: The court modified the lower court's judgment to the extent that it reinstated the taxpayer's action against the city and remanded the matter to the lower court for a determination on the merits. The judgment of the lower court was affirmed as modified.

 

457 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Thoreson v. Penthouse Int'l


43730-43731


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


179 A.D.2d 29; 583 N.Y.S.2d 213; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5427; 59 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1092



April 2, 1992, Decided  
April 2, 1992, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, magazine and publisher, appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which awarded plaintiff model compensatory and punitive damages in a bench trial on her sexual harassment claim under §§ 296(1), 297(9) of the New York Human Rights Law, N.Y. Exec. Law § 290 et seq., and denied defendants' motion to vacate the punitive damages award.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff model brought suit against defendants, magazine and publisher, alleging sexual harassment in violation of §§ 296(1), 297(9) of the New York Human Rights Law, N.Y. Exec. Law § 290 et seq. Following a bench trial, the court awarded plaintiff $ 60,000 in compensatory and $ 4,000,000 in punitive damages. On appeal, the court vacated the punitive damages award but affirmed the compensatory damages award, holding that punitive damages were not available under § 297(9) because by including in the Human Rights Law a provision for the award of punitive damages in cases of housing discrimination only, the state legislature had indicated an intent to exclude punitive damages in all other instances. The court further held that the legislature intended to provide an alternative judicial forum for the determination of claims arising under the Human Rights Law, not to afford relief different in kind and greater in degree from that available in administrative proceedings before the State Division of Human Rights.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the award of punitive damages against defendants, magazine and publisher, but otherwise modified and affirmed the judgment in favor of plaintiff model. The New York Human Rights Law did not contemplate punitive damages because the statutory language and legislative history suggested only that the legislature intended to provide an alternative, judicial forum for the determination of claims arising under the Human Rights Law.

 

458 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Cafe Iguana Corp. v. New York


45610


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


181 A.D.2d 586; 581 N.Y.S.2d 770; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4014



March 24, 1992, Decided  
March 24, 1992, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner cafe owner brought a petition pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, seeking review of the determination of respondent Department of Consumer Affairs of the City of New York, which found the cafe owner guilty of operating an unlicensed cabaret, and ordered the premises sealed in the event the unlicensed activities were not discontinued within 10 days.


OVERVIEW: The court determined that there was no merit to the cafe owner's argument that the padlocking order was in excess of its jurisdiction and arbitrary and capricious. The court held that the fact that only a limited portion of the premises were used for dancing had no bearing on the question of whether the premises were being "primarily" used as a cabaret. The evidence supported the finding that the premises were being used primarily for several activities, none of which under the statute was required to predominate. The court held that there was no merit to the cafe owner's argument that the statute, both on its face and as applied to the facts of this case, was unconstitutionally vague because it did not define "dancing."


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the order from the consumer affairs department, which ordered the cafe owner's premises sealed. The court denied the cafe owner's petition for review and dismissed the action.

 

459 of 992 DOCUMENTS


T.E.A. Marine Auto. Corp. v. Scaduto


91-01046


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


181 A.D.2d 776; 581 N.Y.S.2d 370; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3704


October 15, 1991, Argued  
March 16, 1992, Decided



DISPOSITION: ORDERED that the branch of the petition which is against the appellant is converted into an action to determine adverse claims to real property (see, RPAPL art 15; CPLR 103c) and that branch of the petition which is against the remaining respondents is converted into an action for a declaratory judgment, with the petition deemed a complaint; and it is further,

ORDERED that the appeal is held in abeyance, the matter is remitted to the Supreme Court, Nassau County, to hear and report on the issue of whether either T.E.A. Marine Automotive Corp. or Edward H. Akam were given notice of the tax lien sale by any means other than publication, and the appeal is held in abeyance in the interim.  [***2] The Supreme Court shall file its report with all convenient speed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax deed holder sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Nassau County (New York), in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, which held that notice of a tax sale and notice of the expiration of the period for redemption were defective. The court held that notice to respondent property owner by publication alone was insufficient. The tax deed holder contended that the property owner had actual notice.


OVERVIEW: The property owner was a corporation whose president resided on the property that the tax deed holder purchased at a tax sale. The court found it was unnecessary to address the tax deed holder's argument that service of the notice of the tax sale by publication only was constitutional because there was evidence that the property owner and occupant received actual notice of the sale. Respondent auditor testified that actual notice of the tax sale was mailed to the owner. The court held that certified mail receipts bore the owner's president's signature and showed that the owner had actual notice of the expiration of the period of redemption. The court held that notice on the owner's president constituted notice on the corporation because there was compliance with N.Y. C.P.L.R. 311 and N.Y. C.P.L.R. 308. The court held that the matter was not barred by the statute of limitations because the presumption of regularity of notice given to the property owner was not be conclusive until after six years.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court for a determination of whether the property owner received actual notice of the tax sale.

McCummings v. New York City Transit Auth.


43114-15


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION FIRST DEPARTMENT


177 A.D.2d 24; 580 N.Y.S.2d 931; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2696



February 20, 1992, Decided  
February 20, 1992, Entered



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on March 8, 1990, and order of said court entered on May 14, 1990, affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, New York City Transit Authority (transit authority), sought review of a decision of the Supreme Court, New York County, which denied its motion to set aside the jury verdict finding that an officer of the transit authority used excessive force against plaintiff robber.


OVERVIEW: An officer of the transit authority shot a robber in the back leaving him paralyzed. The robber filed an action against the transit authority alleging excessive force and seeking damages. A jury in the lower court found that excessive force was used and awarded damages. The transit authority filed a motion to set aside the verdict based on an improper jury charge. The lower court denied the motion and the court on appeal affirmed the denial. The court held that the errors claimed by the transit authority were either nonexistent or insignificant and unpreserved. The court held that a reversal would require a rejection of the jury's fact finding and a replacement with the court's own or would penalize the wrong party for unpreserved error. The court held that either result would be an abuse of the court's authority on review. The court held that an objection to a charge must state the matter to which the objection was being made and the grounds for such objection. A general objection was not sufficient. Therefore, the transit authority's "respectfully except, your Honor" was inadequate to preserve for review its disagreement with the jury instructions.


OUTCOME: The court held that the transit authority's motion to set aside the verdict was properly denied and the judgment entered by the lower court, following a jury trial, finding in favor of the robber and awarding him damages was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Trial - Instructions - Justification - Preservation of Issue for Appellate Review

1. In an action to recover for personal injuries sustained by plaintiff when, in the course of the mugging of an elderly man, he was shot by a police officer employed by defendant, defendant's appellate contentions have either not been preserved or do not constitute reversible error, and, accordingly, a judgment in favor of plaintiff is affirmed. Defendant urges that the action should have been dismissed pursuant to Penal Law § 35.30 and the decision of the United States Supreme Court in Tennessee v Garner (471 US 1), or alternatively, that the holding in that case is not germane to the instant situation and, in any event, should not have been retroactively applied to this matter; however, since defense counsel not only did not object to reliance upon Tennessee v Garner (supra), wherein it was held that where an officer has probable cause to believe that a felony suspect poses a threat of serious physical harm, either to the officer or to others, it is not constitutionally unreasonable to prevent escape by using deadly force, but acknowledged that Garner was both controlling and retroactively applicable, defendant may not for the first time before the Appellate Division endeavor to disclaim the relevance and applicability of Garner (CPLR 5501 [a] [3]). Similarly, defendant failed to advise the trial court that it deemed it improper to charge the jury pursuant to the standard of reasonableness of an officer's conduct as enunciated in Tennessee v Garner (supra), and defendant may not now advance such an argument on appeal (CPLR 4110-b).

Master and Servant - Respondeat Superior

2. In an action to recover for personal injuries sustained by plaintiff when, in the course of the mugging of an elderly man, he was shot by a police officer employed by defendant, a judgment in favor of plaintiff is affirmed. Defendant's assertion of qualified immunity is precluded as not having been preserved and on the merits is without substance inasmuch as defendant could be liable under the doctrine of respondeat superior.

Evidence - Documentary Evidence - Transit Authority Regulations

3. In an action against defendant Transit Authority to recover for injuries sustained by plaintiff after he was shot by a police officer employed by defendant when the officer intervened during the course of an assault perpetrated by plaintiff and others, defendant's contention that the trial court improperly permitted the jury to consider defendant's 1982 and 1986 rules and regulations lacks merit. Defendant never objected to the admission of the 1982 regulations, and in any event, the regulations did not impose a higher standard of care than Penal Law § 35.30. As for the 1986 regulations, the court struck from the record all reference to those rules and regulations after plaintiff agreed to withdraw them from evidence, and the court gave adequate curative instructions to the jury.

Sierra Telcom Servs., Inc. v. Hartnett


63378, 63379


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


174 A.D.2d 279; 579 N.Y.S.2d 753; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 909; 30 Wage & Hour Cas. (BNA) 1486; 125 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P57,328



January 30, 1992, Decided  
January 30, 1992, Entered



DISPOSITION: ADJUDGED that the determination is confirmed, without costs, and petitions dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, contractor and subcontractor, brought proceedings pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 (initiated in the court pursuant to N.Y. Lab. Law §§ 220, 220-b) to review a determination of respondent Commissioner of Labor which, inter alia, found that the subcontractor willfully failed to pay prevailing wages and supplements when installing a telecommunications system at a state university.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the proof at the hearing established that the subcontractor's work involved solely the installation of a telecommunications system. The commissioner could properly have concluded that, despite respondent Department of Labor's inability to determine the specific job duties of each worker of the subcontractor, all the workers were entitled to receive, at a minimum, the wage rate for telephone installer, rather than that for electrician-lineman. The university's request for proposal specified the work in sufficient detail to constitute compliance with N.Y. Lab. Law § 220(3-a)(a). The department's investigation, prompted by a letter from an unsuccessful bidder, was not unlawful under N.Y. Lab. Law § 220(7), which permitted the commissioner to cause a compliance investigation to be made on his own initiative. The department's adoption of the wage rates set forth in the local collective bargaining agreement did not represent an unconstitutional delegation of power. Because the subcontractor continued to adhere to its payment practices after being notified that they were violative of N.Y. Lab. Law § 220, the finding of willfulness would not be disturbed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commissioner determination that, inter alia, the subcontractor willfully failed to pay prevailing wages and supplements.

Phil Kriegel Assocs. v. M. Lahm Knitting Mill, Inc.


44998


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


179 A.D.2d 539; 579 N.Y.S.2d 44; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 483



January 23, 1992, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sales representative sought review of a decision of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which granted defendant knitting mill's cross-motion for partial summary judgment and dismissed so much of the complaint as sought double damages pursuant to N.Y. Lab. Law § 191-c.


OVERVIEW: The parties entered into a commission agreement in 1977. In a breach of contract action, the supreme court granted the knitting mill's cross-motion for partial summary judgment that sought to have dismissed so much of the complaint as sought double damages pursuant to N.Y. Lab. Law § 191-c. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that uncertainty as to whether the partially oral and partially written agreement included a provision concerning exclusivity, which was not an essential term in a sales representative's agreement, did not render the agreement unenforceable. The court further held that, because the contract commenced in 1977, it was not subject to N.Y. Lab. Law §§ 191-a, b, c, because those provisions expressly applied only to contracts commenced on or after January 1, 1988.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the supreme court, which granted the knitting mill's cross-motion for partial summary judgment with regard to double damages in the sales representative's breach of contract action.

In re Kailee CC


61426


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


179 A.D.2d 891; 579 N.Y.S.2d 191; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 517



January 23, 1992, Decided  
January 23, 1992, Entered



DISPOSITION: ORDERED that the order is affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father challenged an order of the Family Court of Rensselaer County (New York) determining that his consent was not required for the N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law art. 7 adoption of a child by petitioner adopted parent.


OVERVIEW: A mother became pregnant with the minor child and decided to place the child for adoption. The father challenged the adoption by the adopted parent, and the trial court determined that his consent was not required. The father sought review, and the court affirmed. The court held that the unconstitutionality of N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111(1)(e), which was applied by the trial court, did not require reversal because interim standards had been delineated and the court was able to apply those standards. The father failed to promptly assert his interest and manifest his ability and willingness to assume custody of the child. Also, the father failed to avail himself of any mechanism, legal or otherwise, to timely protect his right to establish a legal and emotional bond with the child. Therefore, his consent to the adoption was unnecessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that the father's consent was not required for the adoption of the minor child by the adopted parent.

 

465 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Dime Sav. Bank, FSB v. State


90-04148


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


174 A.D.2d 173; 579 N.Y.S.2d 679; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 339


November 12, 1991, Argued  
January 15, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended February 11, 1992. Second Revision March 18, 1992.



DISPOSITION: Ordered that the order is reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, the motion is denied, the cross motion is granted to the extent that it is declared that Tax Law § 253 (1-a) (a), insofar as it prohibits the plaintiff from passing on a mortgage recording tax to the mortgagor, is unenforceable as against the plaintiff, and New York State is enjoined from enforcing against the plaintiff so much of Tax Law § 253 (1-a) (a) as prohibits the plaintiff from passing on a mortgage recording tax to the mortgagor, and the matter is remitted to the Supreme Court, Nassau County, for determination of the remaining demands for relief in the plaintiff's complaint, and the entry of an appropriate judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff federal savings and loan association challenged the grant by the Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York) of summary judgment for defendant New York State. The association argued that a state statute, which imposed a recording tax on mortgages but prohibited lenders from passing the cost on to borrowers, was preempted by a federal regulation permitting federal savings and loan associations to pass loan costs on to borrowers.


OVERVIEW: The federal savings and loan association challenged the validity of the state's N.Y. Tax Law § 253(1-a)(a). The statute imposed a recording tax on certain mortgages and prohibited the lender from passing the cost on to the borrower. The association alleged that the statute was preempted by a Federal Home Loan Bank Board (board) regulation permitting federal savings and loan associations to pass on to their borrowers the necessary costs incurred in connection with making the loans. The trial court granted the state summary judgment. On appeal, the court noted that the board's regulatory scheme over federal savings and loan associations preempted any conflicting state law. The state did not challenge the board's authority to preempt its law, but argued that the regulation covered only services rendered by private parties in connection with loan processing and thus did not apply to the recording tax. The court disagreed, noting that the regulation included other necessary incidental services and costs. 12 C.F.R. § 545.32(b)(5). The statute was therefore preempted by the regulation, and the court enjoined its application to the federal savings and loan association.


OUTCOME: The court reversed summary judgment for the state and entered a judgment for the federal savings and loan association enjoining application of the state's statute to the federal savings and loan association because it was preempted by the federal regulation.


HEADNOTES

Statutes -- Federal Preemption -- Prohibition against Passing Certain Mortgage Recording Taxes on to  Borrower

Tax Law § 253 (1-a) (a) conflicts with 12 CFR 545.32 (b) (5), which was promulgated by the Federal Home Loan Bank Board and permits Federal savings and loan associations to pass through to their borrowers the necessary costs incurred in connection with making loans secured by mortgages on real property, by imposing a recording tax on mortgages securing loans for certain properties while prohibiting the lender from passing on this cost to the borrower. Although the State has the power to levy a mortgage recording tax, it cannot, under the guise of this authority, or in the exercise of its police powers, interfere with the lending practices of Federally chartered savings and loan associations, or prevent such lenders from recouping the costs of making loans by passing through the cost of the tax to their borrowers. Accordingly, Tax Law § 253 (1-a) (a), insofar as it imposes a mortgage recording tax which may not be passed on to the borrower, is preempted by Federal regulation and is unenforceable as against Federal savings and loan associations.

 

466 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Duffy v. Wetzler


90-07800, 91-02056, 91-02059, 91-02060, 91-02061


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


174 A.D.2d 253; 579 N.Y.S.2d 684; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 739; 14 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2616


May 21, 1991, Argued  
January 15, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended February 10, 1992.



DISPOSITION: Ordered that the order and judgment (one paper) of the Supreme Court, Queens County, dated June 14, 1990, is modified by deleting therefrom the provisions which (1) declared that the defendants may not assess and collect personal income taxes on Federal pension benefits received in the years 1986 through 1988 which may be still due and owing, (2) declared that the plaintiffs are entitled to a refund of that portion of their personal income taxes which was paid on Federal pension benefits for the years 1986 through 1988, (3) granted the plaintiffs summary judgment on the third cause of action, and enjoined the defendants from collecting personal income taxes on Federal pension benefits from 1986 through 1988, and (4) enjoined the defendants from interfering with or refusing to grant the plaintiffs a refund of personal income taxes paid on Federal pension benefits from 1986 through 1988; as so modified, the order and judgment is affirmed insofar as appealed and cross-appealed from, without costs or disbursements; and it is further, Ordered that the orders are affirmed insofar as appealed from, without [***3] costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers brought suit against defendant officials, arguing that under a recent United States Supreme Court decision construing 4 U.S.C.S. § 111, the state's taxation of pension benefits of federal retirees was illegal. The Supreme Court in Queens County (New York) granted declaratory and injunctive relief to the taxpayers, but denied them class action status and dismissed their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court first held that the standards set by the Supreme Court for determining whether a decision should be given retrospective application had not been overruled by a later case and thus were still viable. Applying those standards, it held that the tax case in question should be applied prospectively, stating that it established a new principle of law by deciding an issue of first impression the resolution of which was not clearly foreshadowed; that retroactive application would neither retard nor further the doctrine of intergovernmental tax immunity; and that the equities surrounding retroactive application preponderated in the state's favor. Thus, it held, the trial court's order awarding refunds and similar relief to the taxpayers should be reversed. It held that the trial court correctly denied the taxpayers' application for class action status, stating that class certification was inappropriate in a case where governmental actions were involved and subsequent plaintiffs would be adequately protected under the doctrine of stare decisis. It upheld the dismissal of the § 1983 claims, stating that qualified immunity provided a basis on which to reject them.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's order to delete the provisions that prevented the officials from assessing and collecting taxes on the taxpayers' federal pension benefits received from 1986 to 1988 and that awarded the taxpayers refunds for the taxes paid on those benefits from 1986 to 1988. It affirmed the remainder of the decision.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Personal Income Tax -- Prospective Application of Decision Holding Tax Statute Invalid

1. A decision holding unconstitutional and invalid former Tax Law § 612 (c) (3) and former Administrative Code of the City of New York § 11-1712 (c) (3), which subjected Federal, but not State or municipal, pension benefits to income tax, should be applied prospectively only, where a curative amendment stated that it would take effect "immediately" and apply to all Federal pension benefits received after a certain date. The decision in question was derived from Davis v Michigan Dept. of Treasury (489 U.S. 803) which established a new principle of law, whose resolution of an "esoteric" problem was not clearly foreshadowed, and there has been no showing that retroactive application of the decision will either retard or further the doctrine of intergovernmental tax immunity in light of the fact that the primary purpose of that doctrine is to protect the Federal Government, not private individuals, from being unduly burdened by State taxation. The equities preponderate in the State's favor given the fact that the old taxing scheme had been in force for 50 years, that a sizeable refund of taxes paid would be inappropriate in the current fiscal climate, and that neither party could have reasonably anticipated the invalidation of the long-standing tax provision. Accordingly, it was improper to have ordered tax refunds to plaintiffs, recipients of Federal pension benefits.

Actions -- Class Actions -- Denial of Class Status in Action against Government

2. In an action to invalidate a provision of the State and New York City income tax, denial of class action status was proper since class action certification is inappropriate where governmental actions are involved and subsequent plaintiffs will be adequately protected under the doctrine of stare decisis.

Civil Rights -- Federal Civil Rights Claim -- Defense of Qualified Immunity

3. In an action to invalidate tax statutes which discriminated against recipients of Federal, as opposed to State and municipal, pension benefits for income tax purposes, rejection of plaintiffs' claims under 42 USC § 1983 was correct. The defense of qualified immunity was available to defendants inasmuch as the right claimed by plaintiffs, recipients of Federal pension benefits, under 4 USC § 111 was not clearly established until a relatively recent opinion of the United States Supreme Court was handed down (see, Davis v Michigan Dept. of Treasury, 489 U.S. 803), thereby shielding the individual defendants from liability for civil damages.

Money Received -- Claim against Government -- Protest Requirement

4. In an action to invalidate tax statutes which discriminated against recipients of Federal, as opposed to State and municipal, pension benefits for income tax purposes, plaintiffs' claim for money had and received was properly disallowed since an appropriate legal protest prior to or at the time of payment is a prerequisite to recovery in an action seeking refunds, and the protest requirement was not satisfied by plaintiffs.

 

467 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Robert O. v. Russell K.


91-02117


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


173 A.D.2d 30; 578 N.Y.S.2d 594; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 190


June 25, 1991, Argued  
January 13, 1992 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Revised February 25, 1992.



DISPOSITION: Ordered that the order is affirmed, with one bill of costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Family Court, Suffolk County (New York) dismissed petitioner biological father's action against respondent adoptive parents to vacate and set aside an adoption. The biological father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The biological father brought an action to vacate or set aside the adoption of his child on the ground that he was not aware of the mother's pregnancy until 17 months after the child's birth and 10 months after the child's adoption was finalized. The father argued that his constitutional rights were violated because he had no notice of the child's birth nor of an opportunity to assert paternity or manifest an interest in parenting the child. The trial court dismissed his petition. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that neither the U.S. Constitution nor N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111-a(2) required that the biological father be given notice of the adoption. Further, the court found that the state had the authority to deny a right of consent to the adoption to the unwed, biological father because he had not come forward to immediately assume a parenting role. Finally, the court found that to allow a biological father to contest an adoption after its finalization on grounds that he was previously unaware of the pregnancy would undermine the state's interest in facilitating speedy adoptions and providing stable homes for adopted children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the biological father's action to vacate the adoption.


HEADNOTES

Adoption -- Consent -- Biological Father -- Lack of Notice -- Fraudulent Concealment

Petitioner, the alleged biological father of a child born out of wedlock, who was not aware of the mother's pregnancy until 17 months after the birth of the child and until 10 months after an adoption of the child was finalized, was not unconstitutionally deprived of due process when he was not notified of the adoption proceeding, or given the opportunity to oppose the adoption. The State can deny a right of consent to unwed fathers who do not come forward to immediately assume their parental responsibilities and can prescribe conditions for determining whether the unwed father's manifestation of interest in his child is sufficiently prompt and substantial to require full constitutional protection. There is no merit to petitioner's claim that he was deprived of his constitutional rights; he never developed a custodial relationship with the child and cannot now pursue his parental interest at this late stage. Further, no fraudulent concealment occurred; there is no evidence of any act on the mother's part after petitioner moved from her home, to conceal the pregnancy or the birth of the child, and she was not required to disclose the identity of the biological father during the adoption proceeding.

 

468 of 992 DOCUMENTS


Kalikow 78/79 Co. v. State


43997


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


174 A.D.2d 7; 577 N.Y.S.2d 624; 1992 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 111



January 9, 1992 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered April 9, 1990, affirmed, with costs and disbursements payable by plaintiff.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the owner of an apartment complex in Manhattan, sought review of an order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which granted a motion by respondent, the state of New York, and intervenor, the tenants' association, to dismiss its complaint for declaratory judgment that the Sound Housing Act, N.Y. Admin. Code § 26-408(b)(5), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The owner of an apartment complex in Manhattan proposed to demolish five buildings with 401 apartments in order to construct high-rise luxury apartments. Most of the buildings contained rent-controlled apartments. The Sound Housing Act, N.Y. Admin. Code § 26-408(b)(5), required the owner first to prove there was no reasonable possibility it could earn an 8 1/2 percent annual return on the assessed value of the property without demolition and development. The owner filed suit for declaratory judgment against the state of New York, seeking, among other things, to declare the Act unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint upon the motion of the state of New York and the tenants' association. On appeal, the court held that the unlawful administration by state officers of a statute fair on its face was not a denial of equal protection unless there was shown to be intentional or purposeful discrimination. Second, the Sound Housing Act was reasonably related to the state's legitimate interests in preventing unreasonable rent increases in scarce housing. Finally, the 8 1/2 percent return on assessment standard in the Act did not violate the Taking Clause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court dismissing the complaint for declaratory judgment by the owner of an apartment complex in Manhattan.


HEADNOTES

Estoppel -- Judicial Estoppel -- Inconsistent Position in Prior Litigation -- Lack of Success in Prior Litigation

1. In an action by a landlord challenging the constitutionality of the Sound Housing Act (Administrative Code of City of New York § 26-408 [b] [5]), which requires a landlord who seeks to demolish rent-regulated apartments to prove that there is no reasonable possibility that it can earn an 8 1/2% net annual return on the assessed value of its property without such demolition, Supreme Court improperly concluded that plaintiff was estopped from challenging the constitutionality of the Act as applied, notwithstanding the fact that plaintiff is currently asserting that the assessment on its property is artificially low, whereas plaintiff had previously filed a petition in another proceeding contending that said assessment was too high, since judicial estoppel may not be asserted as a defense unless it can be shown that the party against whom the estoppel is sought procured a judgment in its favor as a result of the inconsistent position taken in the prior proceeding, and the prior proceeding concerning plaintiff's tax assessment is still pending. Moreover, defendants in the instant action are not the same as the defendants in the tax assessment proceeding.

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation -- Equal Protection Challenge to Statute Limiting Demolition of Rent-Regulated Apartments

2. In an action by a landlord challenging the constitutionality of the Sound Housing Act (Administrative Code of City of New York § 26-408 [b] [5]), which requires a landlord who seeks to demolish rent-regulated apartments to prove that there is no reasonable possibility that it can earn an 8 1/2% net annual return on the assessed value of its property without such demolition, plaintiff's contention that because residential buildings other than 1- to 3-family homes are assessed randomly and haphazardly with no uniform ratio of assessed value to full value of any particular parcel of realty, a burden is imposed unequally on similarly situated property owners, is without merit where plaintiff admitted that its buildings were assessed at a higher percentage of market value than most similarly situated property, thereby acknowledging that it has been more favorably treated on the question of return on actual value than other similarly situated property owners. Accordingly, plaintiff has no standing to complain as its assessment does not cause it any injury.

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation -- Facial Validity of Statute Limiting Demolition of Rent-Regulated Apartments -- Equal Protection

3. In an action by a landlord challenging the constitutionality of the Sound Housing Act (Administrative Code of City of New York § 26-408 [b] [5]), which requires a landlord who seeks to demolish rent-regulated apartments to prove that there is no reasonable possibility that it can earn an 8 1/2% net annual return on the assessed value of its property without such demolition, plaintiff's contention that the Act is arbitrarily administered because of allegedly defective assessment practices fails to state a claim against the validity of the Act on its face, since the failure of taxing officials to assess property for taxation on a uniform standard of valuation as required by the assessment laws is not enough without a showing of purposeful discrimination to establish a denial of equal protection. Moreover, even if the property were arbitrarily assessed to the extent of violating the Equal Protection Clause, the remedy would not be an action challenging the constitutionality of the Act, but one challenging the assessment process under the Real Property Tax Law.

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation -- Constitutionality of Statute Limiting Demolition of Rent-Regulated Apartments -- Due Process

4. In an action by a landlord challenging the constitutionality of the Sound Housing Act (Administrative Code of City of New York § 26-408 [b] [5]), which requires a landlord who seeks to demolish rent-regulated apartments to prove that there is no reasonable possibility that it can earn an 8 1/2% net annual return on the assessed value of its property without such demolition, Supreme Court did not err in finding that there was no facial violation of plaintiff's due process rights since the Act satisfies a legitimate State interest in preserving affordable housing and protecting tenants, and it was not irrational to use return on assessed property value as a standard for hardship relief for property owners.

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation -- Constitutionality of Statute Limiting Demolition of Rent-Regulated Apartments -- Increase in Assessed Value of Property

5. In an action by a landlord challenging the constitutionality of the Sound Housing Act (Administrative Code of City of New York § 26-408 [b] [5]), which requires a landlord who seeks to demolish rent-regulated apartments to prove that there is no reasonable possibility that it can earn an 8 1/2% net annual return on the assessed value of its property without such demolition, plaintiff's contention that the Act creates an irrebuttable presumption that the assessed value is fixed and cannot be raised and, thus, that there is a violation of due process, is unavailing since the property owner may seek an increase in assessed valuation if he is willing to pay higher taxes.

Landlord and Tenant -- Rent Regulation -- Constitutionality of Statute Limiting Demolition of Rent-Regulated Apartments -- No Showing of Unconstitutional Taking

6. In an action by a landlord challenging the constitutionality of the Sound Housing Act (Administrative Code of City of New York § 26-408 [b] [5]), which requires a landlord who seeks to demolish rent-regulated apartments to prove that there is no reasonable possibility that it can earn an 8 1/2% net annual return on the assessed value of its property without such demolition, the 8 1/2% return on assessment standard does not violate the taking clauses of the State and Federal Constitutions. A constitutional violation will not result merely because a landowner is deprived of the most profitable use of his property as long as some beneficial alternative use exists, and there has been no showing that plaintiff has been denied the use of its property. Moreover, rent control has been held not to be a per se taking; the Act advances a legitimate State interest; there is no taking where the owner's earnings are limited by a valuation of property below actual market value as long as the return is not unreasonable, and the Act does not single out a small group of property owners and require them to bear a disproportionate share of an existing problem.

 

469 of 992 DOCUMENTS


New York State Conference of Blue Cross & Blue Shield Plans v. Cooper


63782


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


173 A.D.2d 60; 577 N.Y.S.2d 897; 1991 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16807



December 31, 1991 



DISPOSITION: Ordered that the judgment is affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner health insurance plans commenced a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding against respondent Acting Superintendent of Insurance of the State of New York. The Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), granted the superintendent's motion to dismiss the petition pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7804(f) on the ground that the proceeding was barred by the expiration of the four-month limitations period contained in N.Y. C.P.L.R. 217. The plans appealed.


OVERVIEW: The plans contended the lower court erred in dismissing their complaint which alleged ten causes of action challenging the superintendent's approval of a trust agreement providing for the distribution of excess trust fund moneys as time barred pursuant to the four-month limitations period contained in N.Y. C.P.L.R. 217. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. Initially, it rejected the plans' first argument that the causes of were not barred by the expiration of the four-month limitations period because a continuing wrong was involved. In the court's view the superintendent's acts of approving and upholding the contested provision of the trust agreement were fully completed, separate, discrete acts which did not constitute a continuing wrong against the plans. The court also found no merit to the plans' claim that because the first, second, fourth, and eighth causes of action asserted constitutional violations relating to the taking of property without due process, substantive due process, separation of powers and equal protection, they should have been converted to declaratory judgment actions and were subject to a six-year statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment dismissing the plans' complaint on statute of limitations grounds was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Limitation of Actions -- Four-Month Statute of Limitations -- Challenge to Approval of Trust Agreement by Superintendent of Insurance

1. A petition challenging the approval by the Superintendent of Insurance of a trust agreement providing for the distribution of excess trust fund moneys related to medical malpractice insurance was properly dismissed as time barred where it was brought more than four months after the Superintendent issued the approval (see, CPLR 217). Although petitioner has asserted that the limitations period should begin to run from the date it requested that the Superintendent delete an objectionable provision of the agreement, the limitations period began to run at least four years earlier when the trust agreement became final and binding. The request to delete the objectionable provision did not revive the already expired limitations period. Moreover, contrary to petitioner's contentions, the Superintendent's acts of approving and upholding the challenged provision were fully completed, separate, discrete acts which did not constitute a continuing wrong against petitioner such as would prevent the petition from being dismissed on limitations grounds.

Limitation of Actions -- Four-Month Statute of Limitations -- Challenge to Approval of Trust Agreement by Superintendent of Insurance -- Constitutional Claims

2. A petition challenging the approval by the Superintendent of Insurance of a trust agreement providing for the distribution of excess trust fund moneys related to medical malpractice insurance was properly dismissed as time barred where it was brought more than four months after the Superintendent issued his approval, and although petitioner has raised several constitutional claims concerning the taking of property without due process, substantive due process, separation of powers and equal protection, the raising of those issues does not justify converting the matter into a declaratory judgment action and applying a six-year Statute of Limitations, since the constitutional challenges relate to the Superintendent's approval of the agreement and are governed by the four-month limitations period (CPLR 217). Accordingly, the constitutional claims are time barred.

Limitation of Actions -- Four-Month Statute of Limitations -- Challenge to Insurance Rates

3. Causes of action challenging the rate-setting process for excess medical malpractice insurance coverage are time barred since they were commenced more than four months after the date on which the rates in question became final and binding.

Limitation of Actions -- Estoppel to Plead Statute of Limitations -- Challenge to Action by Superintendent of Insurance

4. In a proceeding challenging the approval by the Superintendent of Insurance of a trust agreement providing for the distribution of excess trust fund moneys relating to medical malpractice insurance, petitioner's claim that the Superintendent should be equitably estopped from raising the Statute of Limitations as a defense on the grounds that the Superintendent concealed petitioner's cause of action by not revealing the agreement in response to petitioner's freedom of information request is without merit since petitioner did not specifically request disclosure of the trust agreement in issue, and, therefore, the Superintendent did not have to disclose such document. Accordingly, as there was no concealment of the cause of action in the manner alleged by petitioner, the doctrine of equitable estoppel is inapplicable.

 

470 of 992 DOCUMENTS


County of Rensselaer v. Regan


63846


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


173 A.D.2d 37; 578 N.Y.S.2d 274; 1991 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16808



December 31, 1991 



DISPOSITION: Ordered that the order is affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state comptroller sought review of an order of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which partially granted a motion by plaintiffs, counties, association, and county coordinator, for summary judgment declaring a provision in the 1990-1991 State Operations Budget directing the comptroller to retain up to 2 percent of the moneys collected pursuant to N.Y. Veh. .& Traf. Law § 1197 to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 1197 offered an incentive to counties to participate in a "special traffic options program for driving while intoxicated" program (STOP-DWI) by providing that all fines, penalties, and forfeitures imposed by the county courts in intoxicant-related offense prosecutions would be diverted from state revenues to the county where the offense was committed and deposited in a special account to fund the local program. However, the 1990-1991 State Operations Budget bill contained a provision directing the comptroller to collect and deposit to the general fund up to 2 percent of revenues received in any court pursuant to the STOP-DWI program. The court affirmed the order of the supreme court; the county plaintiffs had standing because they were asserting a proprietary claim of entitlement to a specific fund, i.e., their entitlement to receive the monies collected by the courts under the STOP-DWI legislation. The provision violated the constitutional constraint of N.Y. Const. art. V, § 1 that the legislature was not to assign to the comptroller any administrative duties except those incidental to the performance of the comptroller's constitutional functions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the invalidation of the appropriations provision on constitutional grounds.


HEADNOTES

Parties -- Standing -- Counties Objecting to Provision in State Operations Budget Directing Comptroller to Withhold 2% of STOP-DWI Funds

1. Counties participating in the "special traffic options program for driving while intoxicated" (STOP-DWI) have standing to challenge a provision in a State Operations Budget directing the State Comptroller to retain up to 2% of the moneys collected pursuant to the STOP-DWI program and deposit them into the State's General Fund, rather than remit all of the funds to the counties, since said counties are asserting a proprietary claim of entitlement to a specific fund, viz., their entitlement to receive all of the fines, forfeitures and penalties collected by the courts in participating counties in proceedings on the offenses specified in the STOP-DWI legislation, and that is sufficient for purposes of conferring standing to challenge the validity of subsequent legislation impairing their entitlement to that fund (see, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1197).

Counties -- Entitlement to STOP-DWI Funds -- Constitutional Duties of State Comptroller

2. A provision in the 1990-1991 State Operations Budget directing the State Comptroller to retain up to 2% of the moneys collected pursuant to the "special traffic options program for driving while intoxicated" (STOP-DWI) and deposit them into the State's General Fund, rather than remit all of the funds to the counties participating in the STOP-DWI program, is invalid since the provision in question violates the constitutional constraint against assignment of administrative duties to the Comptroller not incidental to performance of his constitutional functions (see, NY Const, art V, § 1). The STOP-DWI legislation provides in unmistakable terms that the moneys collected by the courts of record in the participating counties as fines, etc., for prosecution of the covered offenses constitute county, and not State, receipts (see, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1197 [1] [a]), and do not ever come into the hands of the Comptroller (see, Vehicle and Traffic Law § 1803 [9] [a]). Accordingly, the duty of the Comptroller assigned by the challenged legislation is not analogous to his setting off an amount due the State incidental to auditing a claim for payment from State funds, nor is the legislation in question merely a direction for the internal allocation of funds within the State's financial structure. There is no nexus at all between the statutorily imposed responsibility and any auditing or other constitutionally designated function of the Comptroller.

Association of Surrogates & Supreme Court Reporters v. State


44930


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


178 A.D.2d 314; 577 N.Y.S.2d 386; 1991 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16735



December 20, 1991, Released  
December 20, 1991, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, State and state comptroller, sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court of New York County (New York) that, in part, declared N.Y. State Fin. Law § 200(2-b), and 1991 N.Y. Laws cc. 166, § 382; 171, § 1, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants attempted, through amendments to N.Y. State Fin. Law § 200(2-b), to effect a lag payroll upon non-judicial employees so as to offset state budget shortfalls. The court granted plaintiff association's motion to dismiss the appeal taken by the State of an order that declared N.Y. State Fin. Law § 200(2-b), and 1991 N.Y. Laws cc. 166, § 382; 171, § 1, unconstitutional. The obligations established here were created by contract between the parties. N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 209-A(1)(e) required a continuation of those benefits grounded and arising from contract. Because this continuation of benefits clause affected post-expiration of contract rights, it was not in conflict with N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law §§ 201(12), 204(3) or 204-a(1), which were related to pre-collective bargaining agreement requirements. Nor was the continuation of benefits clause repealed or modified by the deferred payroll lag statute. The impairment of contract here was substantial and the deferred payroll statute was not justified as a legitimate means of alleviating the State's fiscal crisis. Further, a severance of the portions of the statute affecting unrepresented employees was not warranted.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal brought by defendants and affirmed the judgment.

Carson v. New York City Health & Hosp. Corp.


44719


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


178 A.D.2d 265; 578 N.Y.S.2d 134; 1991 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16345



December 17, 1991, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital appealed a judgment from the Supreme Court of New York County (New York), which was rendered in favor of plaintiff patient awarding damages for injuries sustained as a result of the hospital's negligent care. The hospital asserted that the trial court unduly intervened in the questioning of witnesses thereby depriving them of a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: The patient was admitted to the hospital due to pain in his lower back, numbness, and a tingling sensation in his arms, but was rendered a paraplegic by the hospital's treatment. The patient filed suit alleging medical malpractice and the trial court rendered an award in his favor. The hospital claimed it was denied a fair trial because the trial court intervened into the questioning of witnesses, and that the jury's award was not reasonable compensation pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5522. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that although the trial court did question numerous witnesses, the questions were intended to clarify the testimony and expedite the proceedings in what was a complex medical malpractice case. Furthermore, the trial court did not interfere with the presentation of evidence or the cross-examination of witnesses, nor did it display bias or prejudice against any party. The court also held that the award did not deviate materially from what was considered reasonable compensation. The patient also asserted that an interest rate of nine percent should have been calculated on the judgment, but the court found no statutory support and assessed a three percent rate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court awarding damages in favor of the patient but held that a three percent interest rate would apply to the judgment interest.
